Infinite Regress: Past Impossibility vs Future Possibility
The author proves impossibility of infinite past regress and possibility of future regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why an infinite chain of accidents is impossible in the past but possible in the future, using the eating analogy as a key illustration.

Core Idea
An infinite chain cannot begin, but it can continue forever.

The author tackles a key objection about infinite regress of accidents. He uses a simple analogy about eating to show that backward infinity is impossible, but forward infinity is not. This distinction is crucial for understanding divine power and creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the two distinct scenarios: 'preceding accident' and 'following accident'.
2
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two cases: one where every accident requires a previous accident, and one where every accident requires a later accident. Understand why the first is impossible and the second is not.
3
Understand the eating analogy
Map the analogy: 'Do not eat a morsel unless you eat a morsel before it' vs 'Do not eat a morsel unless you eat a morsel after it'. Recognise how this illustrates the difference between past and future regress.
The analogy makes the abstract logical point concrete.
4
Apply the analogy to accidents
Connect the eating analogy back to the regress of accidents. The first scenario shows that starting is impossible; the second shows that starting is possible and then continuation is endless.
5
Reflect on Abu al-Hudhayl's error
The author notes that failure to distinguish between past and future regress led Abu al-Hudhayl to an erroneous position. Consider how clarity on this point protects correct theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عرض إلا وقبله عرض مما يعرف بطلانه بالحس، فإنا رأينا عرضا ما موجودا ثم قلنا لا وجود لهذا إلا وقبله عرض ثم كذا ذلك العرض لا وجود له إلا وقبله عرض آخر هكذا إلى ما لا يتناهى وما لا تناهي له لا يتحقق ثبوته فإذا لا يتحقق ثبوت هذا العرض وهو قد تحقق فيثبت أن وجوده لم يتعلق بما لا تحقق له، وبمثله لو قيل : لا عرض إلا وبعده عرض لم يمتنع ثبوت هذا العرض، بل وجوده يقتضي وجودا آخر بعده، ووجود الثاني ووجود الثالث كذا لا إلى نهاية نظيره أمر تضاعف الحساب أنه إذ لم يجعل له ابتداء منه يبدأ لا يجوز وجود شيء منه البتة، وإذا حصلت البداية يجوز أن يبقى فيه فيزيد ثم يزيد دائما وكذا من قال لغيره : لا تأكل لقمة إلا وتأكل قبلها لقمة لا يتمكن من الدخول في الأكل فإن كل لقمة يريد أن يأكلها كان من شرط أكلها أن يأكل قبلها أخرى فيبقى غير آكل أبدا، وبمثله لو قال له: لا تأكل لقمة إلا وتأكل بعدها لقمة أخرى لتمكن من الدخول في الأكل ثم يبقى أبد الدهر آكلا فكذا هذا ، والعجز عن دفع هذا السؤال وتعذر التفرقة بين الماضي والمستأنف ألجأ أبا الهذيل.
No accident except before it is an accident, which is known to be false by sense. For we see some existing accident, then we say: this has no existence except before it is an accident. Then likewise that accident has no existence except before it is another accident, and so on ad infinitum. That which has no end has no verified existence. Therefore the existence of this accident would not be verified, but it has been verified; so it is established that its existence was not attached to what has no verification. Similarly if it were said: 'No accident exists without there being an accident after it,' the existence of this accident would not be prevented. Rather its existence necessitates another existence after it, and the existence of the second and the third likewise ad infinitum. Its analogue is the matter of doubling accounts: when no beginning is assigned from which to start, it is absolutely impossible for anything of it to exist. But when a beginning is obtained, it is possible for it to continue, increase, then increase perpetually. Likewise if one says to another: 'Do not eat a morsel unless you eat a morsel before it,' he is unable to begin eating, because every morsel he wishes to eat has the condition that he eat another before it, so he remains never eating forever. Similarly if he said to him: 'Do not eat a morsel unless you eat a morsel after it,' he is able to begin eating, then he remains eating forever. So it is with this. The inability to repel this question and the difficulty of distinguishing between the past and the future forced Abu al-Hudhayl.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage is a proof against infinite regress in the past but allows it in the future, using an analogy of eating. The author first presents the case of an accident requiring a preceding accident. If every accident must have a predecessor, then an infinite chain backward is impossible because it would never reach a starting point, so the existence of the first accident would never be realized. But since accidents do exist (observed by sense), the chain must have a beginning. Then the author contrasts this with the future: if every accident must have a successor, that does not prevent the existence of the first accident; it only entails an endless future series. This is illustrated by two eating scenarios: one where each morsel requires a previous morsel, making eating impossible to start; the other where each morsel requires a following morsel, allowing a start and then endless eating. The author concludes that the inability to distinguish between past and future regress led Abu al-Hudhayl to his erroneous view.

Key Terms
عرض
ما لا يتناهى
التسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Infinite regress in either direction (past or future) is impossible for accidents.
Correction: Only infinite regress in the past is impossible; infinite regress in the future is possible and even entailed by certain causal relations.

Checkpoint
Why does the author consider an infinite regress of accidents in the past impossible?
A) Because it would entail a violation of sense perception.
B) Because it would never have a beginning, so nothing would exist.
C) Because accidents cannot exist without substances.
D) Because God's power is limited.

Key Takeaway
An infinite chain of causation cannot begin in the past, but if it has a start, it can continue forever into the future.

The lesson proves that an infinite past is impossible — you have a definite beginning. Does your daily life reflect the urgency of this, or do you live as if you have endless tomorrows? What one change in your schedule this week will remind you that your time is finite?
?
The author distinguishes between what can begin and what can continue. Is there a sin or bad habit you are avoiding confronting because you think you need to fix something else first? Identify the 'first morsel' of repentance you are delaying, and commit to performing it before you sleep tonight.

The Contradiction of Claiming the World is Eternal While Dependent on an Eternal Cause
Refutes the first Dahriyya group who claim the world is eternal because God is its cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that the world is eternal because its cause is eternal leads to a logical contradiction, and how the author uses the concepts of qadīm and muḥdath to expose this error.

Core Idea
An eternal being cannot depend on another; claiming the world is both eternal and dependent is self-contradictory.

The author has already established the temporal origination (ḥudūth) of the world with certainty. Now he turns to refute the Dahriyya who argue that the world is eternal because God—whether as cause, bounty, knowledge, power, or wisdom—is eternal. He will show that this reasoning is corrupt, because the eternity of the cause does not necessitate the eternity of the effect, and further, claiming the world is both eternal and dependent on another is a manifest contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how the author begins by reasserting the certainty of the proof for temporal origination before addressing the Dahriyya claim.
The passage builds on the previous proof of ḥudūth.
2
Identify the Dahriyya claim
The first group of Dahriyya assert that the world is eternal because God (or His attributes) is the cause of its existence. Note the variations: cause, bounty, knowledge, power, wisdom.
They mistake the relationship between cause and effect.
3
Grasp the first refutation
The author points out that we have established the temporal origination of accidents through sensory experience. The eternity of God’s essence or attributes does not necessitate the eternity of those accidents. Therefore, the eternity of the cause does not imply the eternity of the effect.
This refutes the claim directly.
4
Understand the deeper contradiction
The opponents admit the world is made (maṣnūʿ) yet claim it is eternal. But an eternal being is independent, while a temporally originated being is dependent. By claiming both, they effectively say the world has no beginning and yet has a beginning—a direct contradiction.
This is the core logical flaw.
5
Note the secondary refutation
The author briefly mentions that the claim of eternal matter (ṭīna) with temporal making has already been refuted, reinforcing that no part of the world can be eternal.
This is a reminder of an earlier proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مضاهية لطريق البرهان في إفادة اليقين وإظهار بطلان ما يقابله من الرأي، وقد حصل ذلك بحمد الله.
الرد على شبه الدهرية:
جئنا إلى حل شبهات الدهرية، فأما القائلون منهم بأنه قديم لأن الباري تعالى علة وجوده أو جوده أو علمه أو قدرته أو حكمته على نحو ما مر من بيان أقاويلهم فهو في غاية الفساد، لأنا بينا دلالة الحدوث، وثبتنا ذلك بما يوجب العلم به قطعا يقينا وفي ثبوت ذلك ظهور بطلان القول بقدمه ألا ترى أنا ثبتنا حدوث بعض الأعراض في الحال على وجه يعرف ذلك بالحس، ولم يقتض قدم ذات صانعه ولا قدم جوده أو علمه أو قدرته أو حكمه قدم تلك الأعراض. وظهر بهذا أن قدم ما به يتعلق بوجود العالم لم يوجب قدمه نحقق ذلك: أن هؤلاء كلهم أقروا بكون العالم مصنوعا ثم ادعوا قدمه لكون ما يتعلق وجوده به قديما، والقديم يمتنع تعلق ذاته بآخر يوجده، وكيف يتصور ذلك وقط لم يكن ذاته غير موجود، والقول بقدم ما تعلق وجوده بغير مناقضة ظاهرة إذ القديم ما يستغني في وجوده عن غيره والمحدث ما يتعلق وجوده بغيره فهم إذا قالوا: هو قديم وقالوا مع ذلك أن وجوده تعلق بغيره، صاروا قائلين أنه قديم محدث وهو متناقض، لأنه يصير كأنهم قالوا: العالم لا ابتداء لوجوده ومع هذا لوجوده ابتداء وعرف بما سبق ذكره بطلان قول القائلين: إن العالم قديم الطينة حديث الصنعة، فإنا بينا استحالة القول بأصل للعالم متعر عن الحوادث.
It resembles the method of demonstration in providing certainty and showing the falsity of what opposes it from opinion, and that has been attained, praise be to God.
The refutation of the doubts of the Dahriyya:
We come to resolve the doubts of the Dahriyya. As for those among them who say that it is eternal because the Creator, exalted be He, is the cause of its existence, or His bounty, or His knowledge, or His power, or His wisdom, in the manner that has passed in the exposition of their statements, it is utterly corrupt. For we have demonstrated the evidence of temporal origination, and we have established that by what necessitates certain knowledge of it. And in the establishment of that is the manifestation of the falsity of the statement of its eternity. Do you not see that we have established the temporal origination of some accidents immediately, in a way known by sensory perception, and the eternity of the essence of its Maker, nor the eternity of His bounty, knowledge, power, or wisdom, necessitated the eternity of those accidents. And by this it has become clear that the eternity of that by which the existence of the world is connected did not necessitate its eternity. We verify that: all of them have acknowledged that the world is made, then they claimed its eternity because that to which its existence is connected is eternal. But the eternal is impossible for its essence to be connected to another that brings it into existence. How could that be conceived, when its essence has never been non-existent? And the statement of the eternity of that whose existence is connected to another is a manifest contradiction. For the eternal is that which is independent in its existence from others, and the temporally originated is that whose existence is connected to others. So when they say it is eternal and also say that its existence is connected to another, they become saying it is eternal and temporally originated, which is contradictory. Because it becomes as if they said: the world has no beginning for its existence and at the same time it has a beginning. And it is known from what has been previously mentioned the falsity of the statement of those who say: the world is eternal in its matter and temporally originated in its making. For we have demonstrated the impossibility of the statement of an origin for the world free from accidents.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the first group of Dahriyya (materialists/eternalists). The author begins by noting that the preceding proof of the world's temporality (ḥudūth) is certain and demonstrates the falsity of opposing opinions. Then he addresses the specific claim: some Dahriyya say the world is eternal (qadīm) because the Creator is the cause (ʿilla) of its existence – whether through His being a cause, His bounty, knowledge, power, or wisdom. The author declares this utterly corrupt because the evidence for temporal origination has already been established. He points out that we have established the temporal origination of accidents (aʿrāḍ) through immediate sensory experience, and the eternity of God's essence or attributes (such as knowledge or power) does not necessitate the eternity of those accidents. Thus, the eternity of that which the world's existence depends on (i.e., God's attributes) does not make the world eternal. The author then unpacks a deeper contradiction: these opponents admit the world is made (maṣnūʿ) but claim it is eternal because its cause is eternal. However, that which is eternal cannot have its existence dependent on another, for an eternal being is self-sufficient. By saying the world is both eternal and dependent, they effectively say it is both eternal and temporally originated (muḥdath), a clear contradiction. It is as if they say the world has no beginning and yet has a beginning. The passage concludes by recalling the earlier refutation of those who claim the world is eternal in its matter (ṭīna) but temporally originated in its making – that too is impossible.

Key Terms
الدهرية
قديم
محدث
علة
حدوث
برهان
أعراض
صنعة
طينة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If the cause is eternal, the effect must also be eternal.
Correction: The author shows that the temporality of accidents is independent of the eternity of the cause; the effect's existence depends on the cause but is not co-eternal with it.

Checkpoint
What is the main contradiction the author points out in the argument of those who say the world is eternal because its cause is eternal?
A) They admit the world is made yet claim it is eternal.
B) They say the world has no beginning but also has a beginning.
C) They say the world is both eternal and temporally originated.
D) All of the above.

Key Takeaway
The world cannot be eternal because it is dependent on its Creator for existence; an eternal being is self-sufficient and independent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that because something comes from God—like a talent, a relationship, or a blessing—it cannot be taken away or change? How does this lesson's distinction between the eternal cause and the temporal effect challenge that assumption? What are you holding onto today as if it were eternal?
?
The Dahriyya wanted the world to be eternal to avoid accountability. In what ways do you treat your life in this world as if it will never end, delaying repentance or good deeds? What step will you take today to remind yourself of your dependence on God and the temporality of this life?
?
If you truly believed that only God is truly independent and everything else is fleeting, how would your priorities shift? What is one created thing you need to release from your heart so that your attachment is only to the Eternal?

The River Analogy: Ignorance of Modality Does Not Negate Proof
Refutes the Dahriyya argument and presents the river analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the Dahriyya argument by showing that ignorance of the modality of creation does not invalidate the rational proof for the world's origination, using the river crossing analogy.

Core Idea
Ignorance of how something happens does not mean it didn't happen.

This lesson presents the first part of Imam al-Nasafi's refutation of the second Dahriyya group, who argue that the world cannot be originated because the process of origination is inconceivable. The author responds by affirming that the world's temporality is already proven by clear evidence, and then introduces a powerful analogy to show that not knowing the mechanism does not negate the reality.

Guided Path
1
Read the Dahriyya argument
Read the first few sentences where the Dahriyya present their case that if the world is originated, the act of origination would lead to an infinite regress or impossibility.
Notice they use a division into possibilities.
2
Identify the author's response
The author states that the world's origination is already established by definitive proof. Then he accuses them of ignorance about the modality.
3
Study the river analogy
Read the analogy carefully. Understand how it demonstrates that seeing a person cross a river proves the crossing even if the method is unknown.
The key point is that denial after direct evidence is obstinacy.
4
Reflect on the application
Apply the analogy to the topic: just as the river crossing is proven, so is the world's origination. Ignorance of how God created does not negate creation.
This is a methodological principle in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما القائلون منهم بأنه قديم ولا صانع له وتعلقهم أنه لو كان محدثا أما أن كان بإحداث أو لا بإحداث والإحداث إما قديم وإما حادث وكل الأقسام باطل. فنقول لهم والله الموفق: إن حدوث العالم بجميع أقسامه قد ثبت بدليل لا شبهة فيه، فبعد ذلك ما تعلقتم به من الكلام فيه بيان جهلكم بكيفية طريق الحدوث والجهل بكيفية طريق شيء ما لا يوجب انتفاؤه عند قيام الدليل على ثبوته، ألا ترى أن من كان على شط نهر عظيم هائل تقرر في ظنه أن لا يتصور للعبور عنه بوجه من الوجوه، وقد رأى إنسانا وراء النهر، ثم رأى ذلك الرجل بعد ذلك في هذا الجانب من النهر لم يبق للرائي شك في أنه غير النهر لا محالة وإن كان لا يعلم كيفية طريق عبوره، ولو أنكر عبوره مع معاينته إياه في هذا الجانب من النهر لما كان أنه لا يعرف كيفية طريق عبوره يعد مكابرا معاندا فكذا هذا، ثم نقول: وجود العالم يتعلق بإيجاد الله تعالى إياه، والإيجاد صفة الله تعالى وراء ذاته أزلية قائمة بذات الباري جل وعلا على ما نبين في مسألة التكوين والمكون وقدمه لا يقتضي قدم العالم لما مر من استحالة قدم ما تعلق وجوده بغيره، ولأن الإيجاد ما كان ليوجد المكون للحال بل كان ليوجد وقت وجوده على ما نبين في تلك المسألة إن شاء الله تعالى.
وهكذا الجواب عن قولهم: إن وجود الشيء لا من شيء غير معقول فإنا أثبتنا ذلك بالدليل العقلي والمعقول ما يعرف ثبوته بالدليل العقلي، وقد ثبت ذلك.
As for those among them who say that it is eternal and has no maker, and their argument that if it were temporally originated, it would either be by an act of origination or not by an act of origination, and the act of origination is either eternal or temporally originated, and all the divisions are false. So we say to them, and God is the grantor of success: The temporal origination of the world in all its parts has been established by an unambiguous proof. So after that, what you have attached of speech about it is a manifestation of your ignorance of the modality of the way of temporal origination. And ignorance of the modality of something does not necessitate its negation when the proof of its existence is established. Do you not see that if someone is on the bank of a great, terrible river, and it is settled in his mind that crossing it is inconceivable in any way, and he sees a person on the other side of the river, then later he sees that same person on this side of the river, the seer would have no doubt that he has crossed the river necessarily, even if he does not know the modality of the way of his crossing. And if he denied his crossing while witnessing him on this side of the river, he would be considered obstinate and stubborn. So likewise this. Then we say: The existence of the world is connected to God's bringing it into existence, and bringing into existence is an attribute of God beyond His essence, eternal, subsisting in the essence of the Creator, glory be to Him, as we will explain in the issue of takwīn and mukawwan. And its eternity does not necessitate the eternity of the world, due to what has passed of the impossibility of the eternity of that whose existence is connected to another. And because bringing into existence was not to bring the brought into existence into existence at the present moment, but rather to bring it into existence at the time of its existence, as we will explain in that issue, God willing.
And such is the answer to their statement: 'The existence of a thing from nothing is not conceivable.' For we have established that by rational proof, and the conceivable is that which is known to be established by rational proof. And that has been established.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage refutes a second group of Dahriyya who assert the world is eternal with no creator. Their argument: if the world were originated (muḥdath), the act of origination (iḥdāth) would either be by an origination or not, and that act would be either eternal or temporal – all possibilities they deem impossible. The author responds by first reaffirming that the world's temporality is proven by clear proof; thus their dialectical doubt merely reveals ignorance of the modality (kayfiyya) of how origination occurs. Ignorance of the 'how' does not negate what is proven, and he illustrates with the analogy of a person on a riverbank who sees someone on the opposite side and later sees that same person on his side – he knows the crossing occurred even if he does not know the method; to deny the crossing would be obstinacy. Similarly, the world's temporality is established regardless of ignorance of its modality. Next, the author explains that the world's existence depends on God's bringing into existence (ījād), an eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence. But this attribute's eternity does not imply the world's eternity, because the world's existence depends on God, and that which depends on another cannot be eternal. Moreover, ījād does not create the world at all times, but rather brings it into existence at its specific time of existence – this will be detailed in the discussion of takwīn (bringing into being) and mukawwan (the brought into being). Finally, he answers the objection that creation ex nihilo is inconceivable (ghayr maʿqūl): what is rationally known to be established by rational proof (dalīl ʿaqlī) is indeed conceivable, and that has been established.

Key Terms
إحداث
محدث
قديم
كيفية
برهان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If I don't know how something happened, it didn't happen.
Correction: Ignorance of modality does not negate proven facts, as shown by the river analogy.

Checkpoint
What does the river analogy illustrate?
A) That rivers are dangerous.
B) That crossing a river is possible only by swimming.
C) That ignorance of how something occurred does not negate its occurrence.
D) That the Dahriyya are correct.

Key Takeaway
The river analogy teaches that rational proof for the world's temporality is sufficient; ignorance of the creative process does not undermine it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you dismissed a clear truth from the Quran or sunnah because you couldn't understand the 'how' behind it? What does that reveal about your trust in Allah's wisdom over your own intellect?
?
The person in the river analogy witnessed the crossing and accepted it. In your life, what undeniable signs of Allah's existence and power have you witnessed, yet you still doubt because you can't explain the mechanism? Will you stop demanding to know the 'how' and submit to the proof?
?
Are you guilty of subtle obstinacy like the Dahriyya—rejecting a truth because it doesn't fit your limited framework? What step will you take today to surrender that attitude, especially regarding matters of divine decree or the unseen?

The Attribute of Ījād: Why the World Is Not Eternal Despite an Eternal Creator
Explains ījād as an eternal attribute and refutes the ex nihilo objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the relationship between God's eternal attribute of bringing into existence (ījād) and the temporal origination of the world, and why the world is not eternal despite that attribute being eternal.

Core Idea
An eternal cause does not necessitate an eternal effect if the effect depends on the cause.

In this second part of the passage, Imam al-Nasafi explains that God's act of bringing the world into existence (ījād) is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence. However, this does not imply the world is eternal, because the world's existence depends on God's volition and is brought into existence at its specific time. He also answers the objection that creation from nothing is inconceivable.

Guided Path
1
Understand the attribute of ījād
Read the statement that ījād is an eternal attribute of God, beyond His essence, and subsisting in His essence.
This will be elaborated in the discussion of takwīn and mukawwan.
2
See why the world is not eternal
The author gives two reasons: the world depends on God for its existence, and that which depends on another cannot be eternal. Also, ījād brings things into existence at their specific times, not at all times.
3
Answer the objection about creation ex nihilo
The objection that creation from nothing is inconceivable is refuted by stating that rational proof establishes it, and that is the criterion for conceivability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما القائلون منهم بأنه قديم ولا صانع له وتعلقهم أنه لو كان محدثا أما أن كان بإحداث أو لا بإحداث والإحداث إما قديم وإما حادث وكل الأقسام باطل. فنقول لهم والله الموفق: إن حدوث العالم بجميع أقسامه قد ثبت بدليل لا شبهة فيه، فبعد ذلك ما تعلقتم به من الكلام فيه بيان جهلكم بكيفية طريق الحدوث والجهل بكيفية طريق شيء ما لا يوجب انتفاؤه عند قيام الدليل على ثبوته، ألا ترى أن من كان على شط نهر عظيم هائل تقرر في ظنه أن لا يتصور للعبور عنه بوجه من الوجوه، وقد رأى إنسانا وراء النهر، ثم رأى ذلك الرجل بعد ذلك في هذا الجانب من النهر لم يبق للرائي شك في أنه غير النهر لا محالة وإن كان لا يعلم كيفية طريق عبوره، ولو أنكر عبوره مع معاينته إياه في هذا الجانب من النهر لما كان أنه لا يعرف كيفية طريق عبوره يعد مكابرا معاندا فكذا هذا، ثم نقول: وجود العالم يتعلق بإيجاد الله تعالى إياه، والإيجاد صفة الله تعالى وراء ذاته أزلية قائمة بذات الباري جل وعلا على ما نبين في مسألة التكوين والمكون وقدمه لا يقتضي قدم العالم لما مر من استحالة قدم ما تعلق وجوده بغيره، ولأن الإيجاد ما كان ليوجد المكون للحال بل كان ليوجد وقت وجوده على ما نبين في تلك المسألة إن شاء الله تعالى.

Why does the eternal attribute of ījād not make the world eternal?

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
You affirm that the world depends on God for its existence at every moment. Is there any area of your life where you act as if you are self-sufficient, forgetting that 'bringing into existence' is an ongoing act? Commit to one concrete change today that acknowledges your total dependence on God.
?
The objection that creation ex nihilo is 'unreasonable' is answered by rational proof. Have you ever dismissed a truth of faith because it seemed 'unreasonable' to your limited mind? What would it take for you to submit your intellect to Allah's revelation, not just in this issue but in all matters of ʿaqīdah?

beginner

The Dialectical Argument on Existence and Non-Existence
Nasafi poses a dialectical question about the non-existent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses a simple logical question about existence and non-existence to expose the contradictions in claiming pre-eternity for anything other than God.

Core Idea
If existence is self-evident, non-existence cannot be a thing.

Nasafi begins by presenting a concise dialectical argument. He asks whether the non-existent was a 'thing' or not, and shows that both answers lead to absurdity when combined with the opponent's own premise that things exist by themselves. This sets the stage for a broader refutation of pre-eternity claims.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation slowly. Let the argument's rhythm sink in before analyzing.
Pay attention to the structure of the question and its two possible answers.
2
Identify the two answers and their refutations
The opponent is asked: 'Was the non-existent a thing?' If they say no, they contradict their own definition that things are things by themselves. If they say yes, then the non-existent would be a thing that is not existent, which is also a problem. Notice how the argument exposes a contradiction either way.
3
Connect to the conclusion about Dahriyya
The author ends by linking this conclusion to the statement of the Dahriyya (materialists), showing that the opponent's view is essentially a version of that doctrine. Reflect on why this link is made.
This step prepares you for the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاعتراض لاغيا هاذيا ثم يقال لهم إذا كان الموجود موجودا لذاته لا لمعنى، وكذا الشيء شيئا لذاته لا لمعنى، أكان المعدوم ذاتا؟ فإن قالوا: لا، قيل: لم كان شيئا والشيء شيء لذاته، وكذا العرض والجوهر، وإن قالوا: كان المعدوم ذاتا قيل لم يكن موجودا، والذات الذي لأجله يتصف بالوجود قائم بظهر بهذا أي قولهم نتيجة قول الدهرية بل هو عين ذلك بل هو شر من قول أصحاب الهيولى بدرجات فإن أولئك ما أثبتوا في الأزل إلا الهيولى وهو شيء متحد الذات عندهم لا كمية له ولا كيفية وليس بجوهر ولا عرض، وهؤلاء أثبتوا جميع أجزاء العالم في الأزل، ثم من قال منهم أن المعدوم جسم في حالة العدم وجوهر أيضا قيل له الجسم هو المتركب، والجوهر ما قام به الأعراض، أكان التركب قائما بالجسم في الأزل والعرض بالجوهر؟ فإن قال: نعم، فقد جعل العرض قائما بالمعدوم وهو محال، وإن قال: لا، فقد أثبت جسما لا تركيب له وجوهرا لم يقم به العرض، وفيه إبطال كون الجسم متركبا، والجوهر حاملا للأعراض، وفيه تصحيح قول المجسمة والنصارى، ولقد صدق من قال : إن المعتزلة مخانيث الدهرية، ووراء هذا للمعتزلة أصول فاسدة أبطلوا بها على أنفسهم إثبات حدوث العالم. وكذا الكرامية وغيرهم من أهل البدع، إلا أنا تركنا ذكرها مخافة التطويل ونشير إلى بعض ذلك إذا انتهينا إلى الكلام معهم في إبطال مذاهبهم، ولأهل الحق طرق كثيرة في إثبات حدوث العالم، أعرضنا عن ذكرها تحرزا عن التطويل وعلما منا بكافية هذه الطريقة. وبالوقوف على هذه الجملة عرف بطلان قول كل من يدعي قدم شيء ما سوى الله تعالى وصفاته مادة كان ذلك أم محلا أم زمانا أم نفسا ناطقة كما يدعي قدمها جماعة من صابئة حران وابن زكريا الرازي المتطبب وكذا بطلان قول من يدعي قدم الأفلاك وما فيها من الكواكب أو قدم الطبائع - فلم نشتغل بالكلام مع كل فريق وإثبات حدوث كل شيء من هذه الأشياء لاشتمال ما أقمنا من الدليل على ذلك كله وبالله المعونة والتوفيق.
The objection is vain and idle. Then it is said to them: If the existent exists by itself not by a meaning, and likewise the thing is a thing by itself not by a meaning, was the non-existent a thing? If they say: No, it is said: Why was it a thing while a thing is a thing by itself? And likewise the accident and the substance. And if they say: The non-existent was a thing, it is said: It was not existent. And the essence by which it is described with existence is subsisting. By this it is clear that their statement is the result of the statement of the Dahriyya, rather it is the same as that, rather it is worse than the statement of the proponents of hyle by degrees. For those (the proponents of hyle) affirmed in pre-eternity only the hyle, which is a thing of single essence according to them, having no quantity and no quality, and not a substance nor an accident. And these (the Mu'tazila) affirmed all parts of the world in pre-eternity. Then whoever among them says that the non-existent is a body in the state of non-existence and also a substance, it is said to him: The body is what is composed, and the substance is what is the locus of accidents. Was the composition subsisting in the body in pre-eternity? And the accident in the substance? If he says: Yes, then he has made the accident subsisting in the non-existent, which is impossible. And if he says: No, then he has affirmed a body without composition and a substance without an accident subsisting in it. In this is the nullification of body being composed and substance being the bearer of accidents, and in this is the rectification of the statement of the Mujassima and the Christians. And indeed truthful is he who said: The Mu'tazila are the effeminate of the Dahriyya. And beyond this, the Mu'tazila have corrupt principles by which they have nullified for themselves the proof of the temporal origination of the world. And likewise the Karramiyya and others among the people of innovation, except that we have omitted mentioning them for fear of length, and we will refer to some of that when we conclude the discourse with them in refuting their doctrines. And for the people of truth there are many ways in proving the temporal origination of the world; we have refrained from mentioning them to avoid length and because we know that this method is sufficient. And by reflecting on this summary, the falsehood of the statement of everyone who claims the pre-eternity of anything other than God—exalted and high—and His attributes becomes known, whether that thing be matter, or place, or time, or a rational soul, as a group from the Sabians of Harran and Ibn Zakariyya al-Razi the physician claim its pre-eternity. And likewise the falsehood of the statement of whoever claims the pre-eternity of the celestial spheres and what is in them of planets, or the pre-eternity of natures. So we have not occupied ourselves with discoursing with each group and proving the temporal origination of each of these things, because the proof we have established encompasses all of that. And with God is help and success.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is a multi-layered argument refuting various heretical claims about the pre-eternity of parts of the world. It begins by presenting a dialectical argument: if existence is due to essence itself, then what about non-existence? This forces the opponent to admit contradiction. Then it contrasts the position of the Dahriyya (materialists) with those who posit pre-eternal atoms (as some Mu'tazila did), showing that the latter is even worse. The author then says that the Mu'tazila have other corrupt principles, but he omits them for brevity. He concludes that with this summary, one knows the falsehood of anyone who claims pre-eternity of anything besides God and His attributes, be it matter, place, time, or the rational soul, and also of those who claim pre-eternity of celestial spheres or natures. The proof he has presented suffices for all.

Key Terms
الموجود
المعدوم
الذات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument only applies to those who say non-existence is a thing.
Correction: The argument covers both possibilities: whether the non-existent is a thing or not, both lead to contradictions.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence if the opponent says the non-existent was not a thing?
A) It validates their position.
B) It contradicts their claim that a thing is a thing by itself.
C) It proves the non-existent is eternal.
D) It aligns with the Dahriyya view.

Key Takeaway
The non-existent cannot be a 'thing' in the same sense as an existent, otherwise it would entail pre-eternity of accidents and substances.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about your own future actions—things that do not yet exist—do you treat them as 'things' in Allah's knowledge? How does that awareness change the seriousness of your intentions and planning before you act?
?
The argument shows that the non-existent cannot be a self-subsistent quiddity without falling into pre-eternity. How does this truth about things that are not yet created affect your trust in Allah's power as the sole Creator of everything that comes into existence?
?
If every non-existent thing is already known to Allah with a determinate quiddity, what does that imply about your accountability for even your unspoken thoughts and desires? How can you make that reality more present in your daily self-awareness?

Causality and Created Things
intermediate
6 min
Refuting Pre-Eternal Matter: Hyle vs. Bodies
Nasafi compares Mu'tazila to Dahriyya and refutes pre-eternal bodies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's argument that the Mu'tazilite position on pre-eternal atoms is worse than that of the materialists (Dahriyya), and why claiming non-existent bodies and substances leads to absurdities.

Core Idea
Claiming pre-eternal parts of the world is worse than claiming a single pre-eternal hyle.

Nasafi now compares the Mu'tazilite view with that of the Dahriyya and the proponents of hyle. He shows that even the materialists only affirmed a single, featureless pre-eternal matter, while the Mu'tazila affirm all parts of the world. Then he tackles the specific claim that non-existence can be a body or substance, and exposes the impossibility of such a view.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Note the comparison between the proponents of hyle and the Mu'tazila. Then focus on the argument about body and substance.
The term 'hyle' refers to prime matter, a featureless substrate.
2
Analyze the comparison
Why does Nasafi say the Mu'tazilite view is worse? Because the hyle proponents only affirmed one pre-eternal entity without qualities, while the Mu'tazila affirm all parts of the world, which is more extreme.
3
Examine the body-substance argument
Follow the conditional reasoning: If they affirm that a non-existent can be a body and substance, then ask about composition and accidents. Both answers lead to impossibility: either accidents inhere in non-existence, or body and substance lose their defining features. This shows the absurdity.
This argument undermines any claim of pre-eternal bodies or substances.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

?

?
Nasafi warns that flawed reasoning can inadvertently support the claims of the Mujassimah and Christians. Are there ways your own arguments about God might be giving ammunition to those who misunderstand His nature?

The Comprehensive Refutation of All Pre-Eternity Claims
Nasafi concludes that his argument refutes all pre-eternity claims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the argument presented in the earlier lessons suffices to refute all claims of pre-eternity for anything other than God and His attributes, including matter, place, time, souls, celestial spheres, and natures.

Core Idea
One unified argument refutes all claims of pre-eternity.

Nasafi concludes by stating that the Mu'tazila have other corrupt principles but he omits them for brevity. He then declares that his presented argument is sufficient to refute anyone who claims pre-eternity for anything besides God, listing various groups and entities. This lesson shows the sweeping power of the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic carefully. Note the author's comment about the Mu'tazila and why he omits other methods. Then focus on the list of entities and groups.
The author is confident that his argument covers all forms of pre-eternity claims.
2
Identify the entities listed
The passage mentions matter, place, time, rational soul, celestial spheres, planets, and natures. Write down each one. Also note the groups: Sabians of Harran, Ibn Zakariyya al-Razi, and those claiming pre-eternity of celestial spheres.
3
Understand the author's strategy
Why does the author not refute each group individually? Because the previous arguments already apply to all of them. Reflect on how the earlier dialectic and body-substance arguments can be applied to any claim of pre-eternity.
This shows the efficiency of the kalam method.

Then it contrasts the position of the Dahriyya (materialists) with those who posit pre-eternal atoms (as some Mu'tazila did), showing that the latter is even worse. The author then says that the Mu'tazila have other corrupt principles, but he omits them for brevity. He concludes that with this summary, one knows the falsehood of anyone who claims pre-eternity of anything besides God and His attributes, be it matter, place, time, or the rational soul, and also of those who claim pre-eternity of celestial spheres or natures. The proof he has presented suffices for all.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
الكرامية
الدهرية
الصابئة
النفس الناطقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument only refutes one specific group (like the Mu'tazila).
Correction: The author explicitly states that the argument refutes anyone who claims pre-eternity for anything other than God, listing many entities and groups.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT listed as something whose pre-eternity is refuted?
A) Matter
B) Time
C) The human soul
D) The divine attributes

Key Takeaway
The proof given suffices to refute all claims of pre-eternity for anything other than God and His attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You may sincerely affirm that only God is eternal, but do your daily anxieties reveal that you treat something else—your career, relationships, or health—as if it must last forever? How does this lesson's claim that all else is temporal confront the idols of your heart?
?
The author says one argument refutes every false claim of pre-eternity. What false 'eternals' do you still entertain in your life—excuses, grudges, or worldly hopes—that you have not yet submitted to the decisive proof that only God endures?
?
If you truly internalized that everything besides God and His attributes is created and passing, what would you change today about your priorities, your regrets, or your possessions? Are you willing to let that change begin now?

The Contingent World Requires a Specific Creator
Nasafi argues that the world's contingency requires a specific cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the contingency of the world necessitates a specific creator and how the world's particularity points to that creator.

Core Idea
The world's contingency and its specific form both point to a deliberate cause.

Nasafi builds a rigorous proof that the world cannot exist without a creator. He begins by establishing that the world is originated, not eternal, and therefore contingent. From contingency he argues that a specifier is needed to bring it into existence. He then adds a second argument based on the world's specific form and qualities, showing that such particularity requires a cause. The passage uses everyday analogies to ground this reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Understand the contingency of the world
Read the first part where Nasafi explains that the originated world is possible, not necessary, of existence. Notice the logical progression: if it were necessary, it would be eternal, but we've proven it originated.
The key term here is 'ja'iz al-wujud' (possible of existence).
2
Grasp the need for a specifier
Study the analogy of the body that can be moving or at rest. Just as a body needs a cause for its specific state, the world needs a specifier to go from non-existence to existence.
The specifier is called 'mukhassis'.
3
Examine the second argument from variability
Read the part where Nasafi argues that the world could have been different in size, quality, etc. This particularity also requires a specifier.
This argument appeals to the modal fact that the world could have been otherwise.
4
Connect to the builder analogy
Notice how Nasafi concludes that this reasoning is used for any building, and denial of it is irrational. Reflect on how this proof is ingrained in human reason.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذ أثبتنا بالدليل أن العالم محدث، فإن المحدث جائز الوجود لا واجب الوجود، إذ لو كان واجب الوجود لكان مستحيل العدم وكان قديما وقد ثبت حدوثه، وإنه قبل الحدوث كان معدوما، دل أنه ليس بمستحيل العدم، ولا بواجب الوجود بل كان جائز الوجود وجائز العدم، وما يجوز عليه الحالان، لا يختص بأحدهما إلا بتخصيص مخصص، كالجسم لما جاز أن يكون متحركا، وإن يكون ساكنا، لم يختص بإحدى الحالتين إلا بمعنى يوجب اختصاصها به وهو الحركة أو السكون فكذا هذا، بل كان العدم أولى به من الوجود لولا معنى بدلت به الحالة؛ لأنه كان عدماً في العدم، وبدلت الحالة بالوجود فلابد من وجود معنى أوجب تبدله ولأن العدم نفي فلا يقتضي تعليلا ولا مخصصا بخلاف الوجود، واعتبر بعدم البناء ووجوده، في مكان مخصوص ولأن العالم يتصور أن يكون على غير هذه الهيئة والقدر ويتوهم أن يكون أكبر وأزين من هذا، ويتصور أن يكون أدون من هذا فكانت هذه الحالة مع ما يخالفانه في الجودة والرداءة والصغر والكبر في حيز الإمكان فاختصاصه بهذه الحالة لا يكون إلا بتخصيص مخصص، وبهذه الدلالة يستدل على وجود الباني لكل بناء يشاهد في الدنيا، وتقررت هذه الدلالة في العقول، حتى إن من أجاز وجود ذلك جزافا من غير صانع له عد متجاهلا في نفسه.
And when we have proven by proof that the world is originated, then the originated is possible of existence, not necessary of existence. For if it were necessary of existence, it would be impossible of non-existence and would be eternal, while its origination has been established. And that before origination it was non-existent, indicates that it is not impossible of non-existence, nor necessary of existence, but rather it was possible of existence and possible of non-existence. And whatever admits of both states is not specified by one of them except by the specification of a specifier, like the body: when it is possible for it to be moving and to be at rest, it is not specified by one of the two states except by a meaning that necessitates its specification with it, which is motion or rest. Likewise is this. Rather, non-existence was more appropriate for it than existence were it not for a meaning that changed the state; because it was non-existent in non-existence, and the state was changed to existence. So there must be a meaning that necessitated its change. And because non-existence is a negation, it does not require a cause nor a specifier, unlike existence. And consider by the non-existence and existence of a building in a specific place. And because the world can be conceived to be other than this form and measure, and can be imagined to be larger and more adorned than this, and can be conceived to be inferior to this. So this state, along with what differs from it in quality and poorness, smallness and bigness, is within the sphere of possibility. Therefore its specification by this state cannot be except by the specification of a specifier. And by this indication one infers the existence of the builder for every building witnessed in the world. And this indication has been established in minds, such that whoever considers its existence as random without a maker is counted as disregarding his own mind.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is a proof that the world requires a specific creator. Nasafi begins by establishing that the world is originated (muhdath), then argues that an originated thing is possible of existence (ja'iz al-wujud), not necessary of existence (wajib al-wujud). If it were necessary, it would be eternal and impossible to cease, but we have proven its origination. So it is contingent: it could exist or not. A contingent thing does not become existent on its own; it needs a specifier (mukhassis) to tip the balance from non-existence to existence. Nasafi uses the analogy of a body that can be either moving or at rest: it needs a cause (motion or rest) to be specified. Similarly, the world was non-existent and then became existent, so there must be a cause for its existence. He also notes that non-existence is a negation and does not require a cause, while existence does. Then he adds a second argument: the world could have been different in size, quality, etc., yet it is exactly as it is. This specification also requires a specifier. He concludes that this reasoning is used to infer a builder for any building, and it is so ingrained in reason that anyone who denies it is considered foolish.

Key Terms
محدث
جائز الوجود
واجب الوجود
مخصص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that contingency alone suffices for a creator, but Nasafi emphasizes the need for a specific cause that specifies this particular existence over alternatives.
Correction: Nasafi shows that contingency only establishes that a cause is needed, but the additional fact that the world has a specific form requires a specifier that chose this form over other possible forms.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why can't the world be without a specifier?
A) Because it is eternal
B) Because it is contingent and could have been different in many ways
C) Because it is necessary of existence
D) Because non-existence requires a cause

Key Takeaway
The world's contingency and its specific attributes both lead to the conclusion that it requires a creator who specified its existence and form.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You were once non-existent, and now you exist. If non-existence does not require a cause, but your existence does, are you living with the awareness that every moment of your existence is a gift from a specific Specifier? What would change if you truly believed that your next breath is not random but given by Him?
?
The world could have been completely different—a different size, shape, or beauty. Yet it is exactly as it is. When you look at your own life—your circumstances, your abilities, your trials—do you see them as random or as deliberately specified by a Creator? Is there any area where you resist acknowledging His purpose in your specific situation?
?
The passage says even a child understands that a building must have a builder. Yet many refuse to see the same in the universe. Is there any part of your life where you are acting as if the world is random, ignoring the evidence of a Builder? What would it mean for you to submit to the Specifier today in a way you haven't before?

Refutation of Self-Creation After Existence
Nasafi gives two reasons why self-creation is impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the world cannot be the cause of its own existence, based on two logical impossibilities.

Core Idea
Self-creation is impossible: it requires existing before creating yourself.

Nasafi addresses a subtle misconception: could the world have created itself after it existed? While this might seem plausible at first glance, it leads to two clear absurdities. In this lesson, we will examine these two arguments and see why self-creation is rationally impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the English translation. Notice the concise style of Nasafi's argument.
2
Identify the two reasons
The passage presents two 'faces' (وجوه) of impossibility. Find each one and understand how they are distinct.
The first reason involves a temporal sequence, the second a logical contradiction.
3
Reflect on the implications
Think about why these two reasons together completely rule out self-creation. Could there be any way around them?
This connects to the broader Islamic theological principle that everything contingent needs a creator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يتوهم أنه أحدث نفسه بنفسه، لأنه إن أحدث نفسه بعدما صار موجودا فهو محال من وجهين: أحدهما وجوده قبل إحداث نفسه لا بإحداث محدث وتخصيص مخصص إياه بالحدوث وهو باطل، والأخر إيجاده نفسه بعدما صار موجودا وإيجاد الموجود مستحيل.
And let it not be imagined that it created itself by itself. For if it created itself after it had become existent, it would be impossible in two respects: one, its existence before its self-creation without the creation of a creator and the specification of a specifier for it with origination, and that is false; and the other, its bringing itself into existence after it had become existent, and bringing the existent into existence is impossible.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage refutes the idea that the world created itself. Nasafi considers the scenario where the world creates itself after it already exists. This is impossible for two reasons. First, it would mean the world existed before its own creation without a creator, which is false because everything originated needs a cause. Second, it involves 'creating something that already exists,' which is logically impossible because creation is bringing something from non-existence to existence. So the world cannot be its own creator.

Key Terms
أحدث نفسه
إيجاد الموجود
محال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the world could be self-caused in a timeless sense, without a beginning.
Correction: Nasafi's argument specifically targets self-creation after existence, but the same logic applies to any self-causation: it would require priority and the absurdity of creating what already exists.

Checkpoint
What is one of the two reasons Nasafi gives against the world creating itself after existing?
A) The world is eternal
B) Creating something that already exists is impossible
C) The world is not a body
D) The world has no will

Key Takeaway
The world cannot be its own creator because self-creation after existence leads to two logical contradictions: uncaused prior existence and re-creating what already exists.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly accept that you did not create yourself and that your existence depends entirely on a Creator, what would change in how you use your time, energy, and resources? What would you stop doing, and what would you start doing?
?
The passage argues that bringing the existent into existence is impossible. In what areas of your life do you behave as if you can recreate or control what already exists (e.g., your past, your nature) instead of surrendering to the One who created you?
?
How would your relationship with Allah change if you meditated daily on the truth that you are not self-made but created by Him at every moment? Write one concrete action you will take this week to embody that dependence.

Human Inability to Change Attributes Proves No Self-Creation
Nasafi uses human powerlessness to argue against self-creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the human inability to alter innate attributes demonstrates the impossibility of the world creating itself from non-existence.

Core Idea
If you can't change your own skin color, you can't create the universe from nothing.

Nasafi presents a powerful analogy: humans, despite their intelligence and dominance over animals, cannot change a single physical attribute of themselves. If they cannot do this, how could the entire world bring itself into existence from non-existence? This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the English translation. Get the flow of the argument before analyzing details.
Notice the structure: claim, human analogy, examples, conclusion.
2
Identify the initial claim
Find where Nasafi states that self-creation is impossible because an act cannot come from non-existence. This is the foundation.
3
Examine the human analogy
List the human capabilities mentioned: subjugating elephants, lions, snakes, extracting from seas and air. Then note the limitation: helpless to change own ugliness, height, skin color.
This contrast is key.
4
Understand the conclusion
Nasafi concludes that if a powerful human cannot change one attribute, then the origin of the world cannot be self-created. Grasp this logical step.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يتوهم أيضا أنه أحدث نفسه في حالة العدم، لما أن وجود الفعل من المعدوم محال، يحققه: أن الآدمي مع أنه ليس بعرض بل هو جوهر، وليس بجماد بل هو نام، وليس بنبات بل هو حيوان وليس بعجم بل هو ناطق. وهذه الحالة النهاية في القوة والتدبير للحيوانات الأرضية، ولهذا يغلب بحيلة اللطيفة وتدابيره الصائبة جميع الحيوانات الأرضية، فيستسخر الفيلة العظام، والأسود الضارية، والحيات الناهشة فيستعملها في حوائجه كيف شاء وأراد، ويستخرج ما في قعور البحار من الحيوانات المائية، ويستنزل من الهواء والطيور الهوائية، ثم هو في حال كمال عقله وعلمه بالأمور، وتمام قوته وبصارته بوجوده الحيل والتدابير يعجز عن تغيير صفة له ذميمة إلى ما يستحليه ويهواه من مضاد تلك الصفة، كالدمامة والحسن، وقصر القامة وطولها، وسواد بشرته وبياضها، فلأن لا يتأتى ولا يتصور إيجاد أصل العالم مما هو معدوم أولى يحققه أن كل عين من أعيان العالم اجتمعت فيه الطبائع المتضادة التي من شأنها التباين ومن طبعها التنافر، ولو تركت وطباعها لتباينت وتنافرت فدل وجودها على خلاف ما يقتضي شأنها أن ذلك ليس من قبل ذواتها بل بقادر لا يغالب وعزيز لا يمانع.
And let it not be imagined also that it created itself in the state of non-existence, because the existence of an act from the non-existent is impossible. Its verification: that the human, despite that he is not an accident but a substance, and not inanimate but growing, and not a plant but an animal, and not mute but rational—and this state is the extreme in strength and management for earthly animals. For this reason he overcomes with his subtle contrivance and correct devices all earthly animals, and subjugates huge elephants, ferocious lions, and biting snakes, and uses them in his needs as he wishes and intends. And he extracts what is in the depths of the seas of aquatic animals, and brings down from the air and aerial birds. Then he, in the state of the perfection of his intellect and knowledge of things, and the completeness of his power and insight with his existence of devices and contrivances, is incapable of changing a blameworthy attribute of his to what he desires and craves of the opposite of that attribute, such as ugliness and beauty, shortness of stature and tallness, blackness of his skin and whiteness. So that the bringing into existence of the very origin of the world from what is non-existent is even more inconceivable and impossible. Its verification: that every individual entity of the world has gathered in it contradictory natures that tend to diverge and are repelled by nature, and if left to their natures they would diverge and repel each other. So their existence contrary to what their nature requires indicates that that is not from their essences but from a Dominant whom none can overcome and a Mighty whom none can resist.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage refutes the possibility that the world created itself from non-existence. Nasafi argues that an act cannot proceed from something non-existent. He then provides a verification using the example of a human being. Humans are the most powerful and clever of earthly creatures, able to subjugate elephants, lions, and snakes, and extract resources from sea and air. Yet, despite their intelligence and power, they cannot change their own innate physical attributes such as ugliness, beauty, height, or skin color. If humans cannot even alter a single attribute of themselves, then it is far more impossible for the entire world to bring itself into existence from nothing. Nasafi adds another verification: the world's entities consist of opposing natures that would naturally repel each other, but they coexist harmoniously. This indicates that their existence is not self-caused but due to an irresistible, invincible Creator.

Key Terms
وجود الفعل من المعدوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does Nasafi use to show that humans cannot change themselves?
A) Their inability to subdue animals
B) Their inability to change physical attributes like skin color
C) Their inability to think rationally
D) Their inability to breathe underwater

Key Takeaway
If humans cannot change even one attribute of themselves, then the world cannot have created itself from non-existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a physical trait you dislike and cannot change. Does your inability to alter it remind you that you did not create yourself? How does this realization affect your gratitude toward the One who created you exactly as you are? Today, will you thank Him for your limitations as well as your abilities?
?
You can achieve great things externally—career success, social influence, even subduing fears—but you cannot change your own inner nature without God. In what areas of your life have you been acting as if you can originate goodness or self-reform on your own? What would it look like to depend fully on Him for that change?
?
This lesson confronts you with your powerlessness: you cannot even change your skin color. If you cannot do that, how can you pretend to be the master of your own destiny? Will you let this truth humble you before God, or will you continue living as if you are self-sufficient? Write one concrete act of surrender you will perform today.

Contradictory Natures Indicate a Creator
Nasafi argues from the coexistence of contradictory natures to a Creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the coexistence of opposing natures in the world proves the existence of a Creator beyond the world's own power.

Core Idea
Opposing natures can't unite by themselves; their harmony points to a Dominant Power.

Nasafi presents a second verification: every entity in the world contains contradictory natures that naturally repel each other. Yet they exist together in harmony. This can only be due to an external, invincible Creator. This lesson examines that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English together. Note the logical structure: claim, explanation of natures, and conclusion.
2
Identify the concept of 'contradictory natures'
Find the phrase 'طبائع متضادة' and understand that these are opposing qualities like hot and cold, wet and dry, etc.
These natures naturally diverge.
3
Understand the implication
If left to themselves, these natures would separate and destroy the entity. Their coexistence is against nature.
4
Recognize the external cause
Nasafi concludes that the existence of harmony indicates a Dominant, Mighty Creator who holds them together.
This Creator is 'قادر لا يغالب' and 'عزيز لا يمانع'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يتوهم أيضا أنه أحدث نفسه في حالة العدم، لما أن وجود الفعل من المعدوم محال، يحققه: أن الآدمي مع أنه ليس بعرض بل هو جوهر، وليس بجماد بل هو نام، وليس بنبات بل هو حيوان وليس بعجم بل هو ناطق. وهذه الحالة النهاية في القوة والتدبير للحيوانات الأرضية، ولهذا يغلب بحيلة اللطيفة وتدابيره الصائبة جميع الحيوانات الأرضية، فيستسخر الفيلة العظام، والأسود الضارية، والحيات الناهشة فيستعملها في حوائجه كيف شاء وأراد، ويستخرج ما في قعور البحار من الحيوانات المائية، ويستنزل من الهواء والطيور الهوائية، ثم هو في حال كمال عقله وعلمه بالأمور، وتمام قوته وبصارته بوجوده الحيل والتدابير يعجز عن تغيير صفة له ذميمة إلى ما يستحليه ويهواه من مضاد تلك الصفة، كالدمامة والحسن، وقصر القامة وطولها، وسواد بشرته وبياضها، فلأن لا يتأتى ولا يتصور إيجاد أصل العالم مما هو معدوم أولى يحققه أن كل عين من أعيان العالم اجتمعت فيه الطبائع المتضادة التي من شأنها التباين ومن طبعها التنافر، ولو تركت وطباعها لتباينت وتنافرت فدل وجودها على خلاف ما يقتضي شأنها أن ذلك ليس من قبل ذواتها بل بقادر لا يغالب وعزيز لا يمانع.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

In that struggle, do you honestly rely on the One who holds natures together, or do you try to manage the conflict yourself? What would it look like to consciously entrust that tension to the 'Dominant whom none can overcome'?
?
When you look at the stability of your own body—heart beating, cells functioning despite conflicting chemical processes—do you see it as a sign of Allah's power, or do you take it for granted? How can you train yourself to see His hand in every moment of harmony around you?
?
The passage says that if things were left to their natures, they would disintegrate. What areas of your life (health, relationships, faith) are currently 'stable' only because of His mercy? What would happen if He withdrew His hold for an instant? Let that sobering thought lead you to immediate gratitude and reliance on Him alone.

The Rational Argument for Permissibility
Nasafi builds a rational argument for permissibility using sheep's helplessness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument that permitting the slaughter of sheep is necessary for preserving the species.

Core Idea
Permitting consumption of sheep saves the species from extinction.

Nasafi addresses a doubt by presenting a simple observation: sheep are defenseless and dependent on humans. Without the incentive to use them, humans would not protect them, leading to extinction. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the empirical premise
Read the opening sentences: sheep have no natural defenses (no legs/wings/weapons) and become helpless when away from human care. Note the two detailed scenarios about predators and thirst.
Nasafi uses observable facts to build his argument.
2
Trace the logical consequence
If humans are not allowed to benefit from sheep (eating them), they would have no motive to protect them. Therefore, predators and starvation would wipe out the species.
This is a cause-and-effect chain.
3
Conclude: permissibility preserves
Thus, permitting consumption actually protects the species; forbidding it would be destructive. Nasafi condemns those who would not allow partial destruction to avoid total annihilation.
This is the core of the rational argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبهتهم، وبالله التوفيق والعصمة . ثم يقال لهم : إن الجنس الذي جعل غذاء للبشر من جملة الحيوانات هو الغنم، ومن المعلوم الذي لا ريب فيه أن هذا الجنس لو خلا عن قيام الآدمي بدفع أسباب الهلاك عنه، وإيصال ما فيه منفعته ومصلحته إليه، ولا امتناع له لا بالقوائم ولا بالجناح، وليس معه آلة الدفاع والحراب فتمزقه السباع من أوهى مدة أسرع وقت، وكذا من طبع هذا الجنس أن راعيها لو بعد عنها في المفاوز والصحاري لبقيت رافعة رؤوسها إلى السماء متخوفة عن كل صوت، نافرة عن كل ذكر لا تتناول علفا، ولا ترد ماء إلى أن تتلف جوعا وعطشا، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك، فلو لم يبح للآدمي الانتفاع بها وتناول لحومها، لما قام بالدفع عنها والحفظ لها فيتلف الكل وينقطع الجنس، فكان إباحة التناول إبقاء للجنس، وفي الحظر إهلاكه، فمن لم يبح إتلاف البعض ليصير ذلك طريقا إلى فناء الكل فلا علاج لجهله وحمقه، ثم التقرب بالقرابين كل ذلك بطريق الفداء عن نفسه إذ الله تعالى على كل أحد من خلقه نعمة الإيجاد فشكره يكون بإعدام نفسه طلبا لمرضاته، كما كان شكر نعمة المال بإزالة بعضه عن نفسه، شكر نعمة المنكح والمأكل والمشرب الامتناع عنها بالصوم، إلا أن كل واحد منهم، لو أتلف نفسه شكرا لنعمة الوجود، لانقطع النسل والبشر، وتفانى الخلق وارتفع الجنس المقصود من الخلائق، فاكتفى الصانع بكمال حكمته بفدية يفديها عن نفسه، كما في حق الذبيح عليه السلام ثم هذا كله منا تبرع، إذ لا حاجة بنا إلى بيان شيء من هذا
Their doubt, and with Allah is success and protection. Then it is said to them: The species which was made food for humans among the animals is sheep. It is known without doubt that if this species were left without humans undertaking to repel causes of destruction from it and bringing to it what benefits it, and it has no defense neither with legs nor with wings, and has no tool of defense and weapon, then the beasts of prey would tear it apart in the weakest time and quickest moment. Also, from the nature of this species is that if its shepherd were far from it in deserts and wastelands, it would remain raising its heads to the sky, fearful of every sound, startled from every male, not taking fodder nor returning to water until it perishes from hunger and thirst. And if the matter is such, then if humans were not permitted to benefit from it and consume its meat, they would not stand to defend it and protect it, so the entire species would perish and become extinct. Thus, permitting consumption is preservation of the species, and forbidding it is its destruction. Whoever does not permit the destruction of some so that that becomes a way to the annihilation of all has no remedy for his ignorance and foolishness. Then, drawing near through sacrifices – all of that is by way of ransom for oneself, for Allah Almighty has upon every one of His creatures the grace of existence. So gratitude for it is by annihilating oneself seeking His pleasure, just as gratitude for the blessing of wealth is by removing some of it from oneself, gratitude for the blessing of marriage and food and drink is by refraining from them through fasting. However, if each one of them were to destroy himself in gratitude for the blessing of existence, then offspring and humanity would cease, the creation would perish, and the intended species among creatures would be removed. So the Maker, in the perfection of His wisdom, sufficed with a ransom that one offers for himself, as in the case of the sacrificed one (peace be upon him). Then all of this from us is a voluntary gift, for we have no need to explain any of this.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage presents a twofold argument: first, a rational proof that the permissibility of slaughtering sheep is necessary for preserving their species; second, a theological explanation of sacrifice as a ransom for oneself, which prevents self-annihilation in gratitude to God.

The passage begins by addressing a doubt (likely of dualists or opponents) and asserts reliance on God for success. It then presents an empirical observation: sheep are defenseless—no claws, wings, or weapons—and if left alone, predators would quickly destroy them. Moreover, sheep become so fearful away from human care that they refuse food and water and die. Therefore, if humans were not permitted to eat them, they would have no incentive to protect them, leading to the species' extinction. Hence, allowing consumption actually preserves the species, while forbidding it would destroy it. The author condemns as foolish anyone who would forbid killing some individuals if that leads to the extinction of the whole.

The second part links this to the concept of sacrifice (qurban). Gratitude for God's gift of existence would logically require annihilating oneself, but this would destroy humanity. So God, in His perfect wisdom, instituted a ransom (fidya) through sacrifice, as illustrated by the story of the sacrificed one (Ishmael or Isaac). However, the author concludes that all this is voluntary (tabarru'), because they have no need to explain such details, suggesting that the main argument suffices.

Key Terms
جنس
غذاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Slaughtering animals is wasteful and harmful to the species.
Correction: Nasafi argues that permissibility of slaughter actually preserves the species by ensuring human protection; prohibition would lead to extinction.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what would happen if humans were not permitted to eat sheep?
A) Sheep would thrive without human interference.
B) Humans would protect them out of kindness.
C) The species would become extinct.
D) Sheep would learn to defend themselves.

Key Takeaway
Permitting the slaughter of sheep is a means of preserving the species, not destroying it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you eat meat, do you ever pause to consider that your consumption is part of God's wise plan to preserve that species? How does that change your attitude toward your meal?
?
Have you ever been quick to forbid something you thought was harmful, only to later realize that the greater harm lies in prohibiting it? What can you learn from this lesson about being cautious in issuing judgments?
?
If you are honest, does the thought that your daily food choices are tied to divine preservation of life ever cross your mind? What would it take for you to develop that constant awareness?

Sacrifice as Ransom for Gratitude
Nasafi explains sacrifice as a ransom that replaces self-annihilation in gratitude.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how sacrifice (qurban) serves as a merciful substitute for the logical requirement of self-annihilation in gratitude to God.

Core Idea
Sacrifice replaces self-destruction as a way to thank God for existence.

In this continuation, Nasafi explains the deeper wisdom behind sacrificial rituals. He draws an analogy: gratitude for wealth is shown by giving some away, so gratitude for existence would require giving life itself—but that would destroy humanity. Therefore, God instituted sacrifice as a ransom.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle of gratitude
Read how gratitude for various blessings (wealth, food, marriage) is expressed by parting with some of them. So gratitude for existence would logically require sacrificing one's own life.
Nasafi uses an analogy to show consistency.
2
Recognize the problem of self-annihilation
If everyone destroyed themselves in gratitude, humanity would cease to exist. This would contradict the purpose of creation.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
3
Appreciate the solution: ransom
God, in His wisdom, allowed animal sacrifice as a ransom (fidya) to substitute for self-annihilation, as was done with the sacrificed one (Ishmael/Isaac).
Thus sacrifice is a divine mercy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Dilemma of the Servant's Recitation and Abu al-Husayn's Attempted Solution
Author presents a dilemma and then gives Abu al-Husayn al-Basri's attempted solution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the dilemma posed to the Mu'tazilites regarding the servant's recitation and Abu al-Husayn al-Basri's attempted solution based on Arabic language conventions.

Core Idea
The servant's recitation forces a dilemma: either it is his act or not, both problematic for the Mu'tazilites.

This passage presents a powerful dilemma against the Mu'tazilite position on the servant's recitation. The author shows that if the recitation is not the servant's act, they fall into pure disbelief; if it is the servant's act, they cannot explain what God's speech is. Then, Abu al-Husayn al-Basri offers a linguistic escape.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to get the flow of the argument.
The passage ends abruptly mid-sentence; note the incomplete example.
2
Identify the two horns of the dilemma
Find the two alternatives presented: either the recitation is not the servant's act, or it is the servant's act and not God's speech.
3
Understand the consequence of each horn
The first horn leads to agreeing with Jahm (pure disbelief). The second horn forces them to abandon their school. Note the rhetorical question that follows.
The author uses Abu al-Hudhayl's quote to emphasize the severity of the first horn.
4
Examine Abu al-Husayn's attempted solution
Abu al-Husayn al-Basri tries to resolve the dilemma by appealing to Arabic: speech is attributed to the first speaker in a real sense.
The passage cuts off before completing the example; consider what the full argument might be.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: إن هذه القراءة الحاصلة من العبد بعد أن لم تكن بقرأته واختياره وقصده إلى تحصيله، ليس بفعل العبد وليس بكلام له، فقد سدوا على أنفسهم طرق إثبات الفعل للعباد، ووافقوا جهما في ذلك كفرا محضا زائدا رتبته على رتبة تشبيه الله تعالى بخلقه على ما حكوا عن أبي الهذيل العلاف رئيسهم أنه كان يقول : المجبرة شر من المشبهة. وإن زعموا أنه فعل العبد وكلامه وليس بكلام الله تعالى، فقد تركوا مذهبهم. وقيل لهم : فكلام الله إذا ما هو؟ ولا سبيل لهم إلى إثباته وتصوره. وأراد أبو الحسين البصري الانفصال عن هذا الكلام فزعم أن اللغة العربية تقتضي إضافة الكلام إلى أول من تكلم به على سبيل الحقيقة، ألا ترى أنا إذا سمعنا
If they say: This recitation produced by the servant, after it was not by his reading, choice, and intention to obtain it, is not the act of the servant and is not his speech, then they have blocked upon themselves the ways of proving the act for the servants, and they have agreed with Jahm in that, which is pure disbelief, whose rank exceeds the rank of likening Allah to His creation, according to what they narrated from Abu al-Hudhayl al-'Allaf, their leader, that he used to say: 'The Jabriyya are worse than the Mushabbiha.' And if they claim that it is the act of the servant and his speech, and it is not the speech of Allah, then they have abandoned their school. And it was said to them: What then is the speech of Allah? And they have no way to prove it or conceive it. And Abu al-Husayn al-Basri wanted to separate from this speech, so he claimed that the Arabic language necessitates attributing speech to the first speaker in a real sense. Do you not see that if we hear...
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This passage is a dilemma followed by an attempted solution. The author presents two alternatives to the Mu'tazilites regarding the servant's recitation: either it is not the servant's act (which would align them with Jahm's determinism, considered pure disbelief by their own leader Abu al-Hudhayl), or it is the servant's act and not God's speech (which forces them to abandon their doctrine that the recited Quran is God's speech). A rhetorical question is then posed: what is God's speech? They have no way to prove or conceive it. Finally, the opinion of Abu al-Husayn al-Basri is introduced: he tried to separate from this difficulty by claiming that the Arabic language attributes speech in a real sense to the first speaker. The passage ends abruptly before completing his example.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The dilemma shows a flaw in the Maturidi position.
Correction: The dilemma is actually a refutation of the Mu'tazilite position, forcing them into contradiction.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilites face an inescapable dilemma regarding the servant's recitation, and Abu al-Husayn's linguistic attempt to resolve it is presented but left incomplete.

Causality and Created Things
